O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications. And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
And because the practical application of medical knowledge is lacking in our region and has been completely abandoned by all, the science has perished and disappeared, leaving only the small written descriptions in books from ancient times that have been handled by the hands. And it is due to this lack of practical application that errors and falsehoods have arisen, knowledge and understanding have been clouded, and the scientific field has been neglected.
It seems to me that I wish to gather together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will gather together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, and the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation as is necessary.
And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been abandoned. And it is necessary for one who practices it to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that they may know precisely the members and their forms, and their connections and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and the number thereof, and their movement and repose, and where they originate.
And so Hippocrates says that a name without the deed is much, and with the deed is little; and the same goes for the art of handicraft.[Note: "art of hand" is a possible interpretation of "l'art de main"]
We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the previously mentioned things should be cautious not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries in her neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman died in his arms.
And I saw another doctor who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large. He brought with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and I knew that if he were operated on, he would die.
And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and did not leave any bandage at the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he commanded him not to loosen it; and it remained so until the leg became entirely swollen and the foot came to perdition.
I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had undone it, he was well and felt no pain.
But still the corruption (gangrene) had already set in the member (leg), and I could not heal it; and the corruption continued to spread throughout the member until the member was entirely lost.
And see one other physician who lanced a hardened abscess and then inflamed it through the malice of his handling.
Because chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron if it cannot entirely remove what is corrupt.
And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, surgery where there is danger in many situations; and I will point out in each place in this book where there is fear and danger.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to be careful so that foolish fools cannot speak ill of you.
So take up your weapons in cotton (?), and undertake your patients lightly and resolutely, and use the best approach so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave behind fearsome diseases with serious health consequences; and put aside your weapons from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other world of glory.
Galen says in one of his teachings: «Do not treat serious illness if you do not want to be called a foolish doctor.»
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter deals with fire cauteries and medical cauteries, and is organized from head to toe; it covers the shapes of instruments, cautery irons, and everything necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, cupping glasses, wounds, the extraction of arrows, and similar things, and it includes descriptions of the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged according to the joints from head to feet, and the shapes of the instruments.
Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is appropriate that I speak of the quality and harm of each complexion.
I say that the quality of help and harm is a lengthy and subtle science and secret knowledge; and about this, many wise people have spoken and agreed; but their words satisfy me little because I dread their length.
I say that the cautery helps universally in every complexion where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter and the dry complexion without matter.
In a hot and dry temperament, some have divided and said that cautery is of great help; and the others said the contrary: that cautery is of no use for a disease that comes from heat and dryness.
For fire's nature is hot, and should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the contrary says that cautery brings great help to a hot and dry disease in the human body. Because when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body to be cold.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And in no way should one meddle with it unless it is someone who has tested it, and who knows through long experience the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and their outcomes and the species of time; we are not afraid of other complexions, even in cold and moist diseases. And all the doctors gathered and agreed on the cautery.
And know, son, that a fire cautery gathers together heat and is of greater benefit than a burning medical cautery.
For fire is simple and does not come to any member except the one that needs it, and does not harm any other member if it is applied carefully.
Hot medicaments move from one member to another while spreading apart, and they bring illnesses with difficult healing to the afflicted part and possibly kill the patient.
Fevers, due to their intensity and the goodness of their substance, do not cause any harm if there is no excess or superfluity.
And this I have found through experiment and the length of service and study that I have devoted to the art, which is close to the truth of matters. Therefore, I excuse myself for the length of my words, as I do not wish to take away from you the secrecy contained within fire, and its quality of work, how it dispels diseases in bodies, just as the philosopher says in his demonstration. Now, receive this in your thoughts.
And know, my son, that they agreed on when cauteries should be performed and chose priests.
And I say that cautery is appropriate at all times, because the harm arising is placed beneath through the aid of cauterization; and even if the cautery is necessary due to urgent and rapid pain that cannot wait for the time it takes for greater evil to come to the limb.
And do not think, dear child, as foolish men do; because the illness that is healed by cautery will not return; and they say so; but it is not as they think, because cauterization is not a medicine that changes complexion, and dries up the humors which are the cause of pain, rather it is a quick medicine due to its power and effectiveness.
And it is possible that the illness comes at times according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the disease and its virtue; and impurities are gathered in him due to the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauterization is administered where there is little excess and moisture, such as cautery for toothache and similar things, and that pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cautery is called the "rear guard" of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cautery has any value after medication, but their understanding is false, and cautery is the "rear guard" of medicine because when we administer methods of cures for any illness and they are not effective, then we administer cautery, and it is effective. Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish doctors.
The ancients said that cautery with an instrument of gold is more gentle than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the place of cauterization does not cause mortification, but that is not true, for I have tried it and found it to be true in some men; and cautery with gold is more gentle than iron, as they rightly said.
And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot because of the color of the gold and it quickly cools down; and if it is heated too much, it becomes brittle in the fire; and so there are many difficulties with this.[**Prompt**: Translate the following text into English.
And for this reason, we use iron cautery which we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter on dislocations from head to feet, so that the vein may be easier to find.
olive cautery
This cautery is useful for moistening and cooling the brain, and it is made for a disease called "soda," as well as for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for an abundance of dreams, pain in the teeth, and sore throat, and also for all illnesses that come from coolness, such as paralysis and stiffness and apoplexy and similar diseases.
The shape of this cautery is such that the patient must be purged with a cleansing medicine that cleanses the head three or four nights, depending on the strength and age and custom of the patient's body; and then warm the patient's head.
And then make the patient sit cross-legged between your hands, and place their hands on a weight; then put the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and place your middle fingers where the tears come out. Warm the "olivare" cautery, which is shaped as follows:
And place it (the mark) on the spot where it is dislocated, and make a sign with ink by pulling down and stretching out your hand repeatedly; then lift your hand immediately, and look at the spot to see if you see a small swelling; and if you do not see it, then repeat the cauterization until you see the swelling as I have told you; after take a small amount of fat, and put it in a soft cloth and place it on the spot, and leave it for three days; after put a wet compress soaked in butter on it; and leave it on until the burn has healed; after cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" until it is healed.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges itself; and therefore, movement helps.
And some of them said that one should leave the cauterization in place long enough that part of the bone is burnt, and then remove what has been burnt from the bone, and then cure it.
And others said that one should leave the cauterization in place for so long and press down so hard that it sinks into the bone as wide as a distaff that women put in their flax, so that the humors can come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one should cure and suture it.
And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is fear; and it seems to me that I should abandon the other one; for the head is weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we witness in other members; and even when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cauterization is more healthy and effective for me, and of this one I use work for a speedy recovery.
of the old pain in the head
When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use roots and pills which are called "cochie", and purgatives for the head and eyes and poultices; and if one applies the cautery that we have previously mentioned and it is not effective.
Take care if the patient's head is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize it a little below the cautery that we have mentioned above.
After perform cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as stated before, and perform a cautery at the spot called "vasselz"; and this is a location where one can apply cupping glasses; and arrange your hand so that you do not see up to the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery than in the others, and I will speak of that later; and the cauteries of the horns should be more refined than those used for the middle of the head, and this is the method.
of the cautery of the head When there is sudden pain in a part of the head, and the illness extends up to the eye, and the head has been purged with cleansing medicines, and the other cures that I mentioned in the division of diseases have been attempted, and yet none are effective: then one performs cautery in two ways, namely using medicine and fire.
The cautery of medicine ague is as follows: take a piece of aloe wood, remove the bark and soak it in a little wine for two days, then apply it to the temple where the pain resides in such a way that you can place the piece of aloe wood under the skin; when it is in place, bind and secure it well and leave it for twelve hours; then undo it and remove the piece of aloe, leaving the wound open for two or three days; then apply a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
After the care of wound healing until it is healed; and if you wish, use any burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
The fire cautery is of this kind. Heat the cautery to the following shape:
And it is called "clos" because the end is shaped like a bell with one curved hollow portion and a small projection in the middle; place it on the painful area and hold your hand steady while moving the cautery lightly back and forth until half of its thickness has been burnt, then lift your hand so that the artery (which is located further out) does not get burned, allowing for an abundant flow of blood.
Afterward, place a piece of cotton soaked in oil on it and leave it for three days; then apply moistened cotton with butter, and continue to care for the wound until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this migraine with the "cultellare" cautery, do so at the very tip, being careful not to touch the artery in this new (not ancient) migraine.
of a headache
When you treat a headache as we have previously said in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help at all, and you see that the cautery before spoken of by medicine and fire is not sufficient, then you should heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it turns white; and place it above the painful area in a straight line half a finger long, and remove your hand once, and hold firmly so as not to cover the artery or reach the bone; and be aware of the movement of the jaw when chewing, and the nerve should not move and spasms should not come upon the patient, and be aware of blood loss from the artery when it is cut, or fear greatly even for one who does not know and is not a learned and experienced person; and leave the work half-finished; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you where it fits in this book.
And if you see that these cauteries do not suffice for the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize it on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if necessary, use the cautery we mentioned in the chapter on arrow extraction, with a cautery having two blades; and this cautery is better than the previous one and more helpful.
of ear pain due to cold draughts.
When pain comes to the ear from cold, and medical solutions and other cures have been tried, as we have said in the division, and the pain does not lessen, then heat this poker-like cautery, called "poins", of which this is the shape:
Afterward, cauterize all around the affected ear, or around both if the pain persists in both, and move back a bit above the root of the ear after you have marked the spot to be cauterized. Then make ten cautery marks around each ear; afterward, care for the area until it heals completely.

of epilepsy
Epileptics should not use cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to cleanse the brain first with purgatives and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medication.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make them gargle and chew purgatives frequently to cleanse the brain with good foods; then let the king's touch be applied in the middle of the head, and perform one cautery on the scalp and one cautery on each horn (temple); and if the patient is strong and able to tolerate it, perform cauteries as I have said for those with paralysis and weakening of the body, on the spine of the back and neck, and let the cautery be made of olive wood in the manner that I have said.

of the fluid from within the eyes
When you administer the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient three rooster combs to drink; then raise the head of the sick person, and apply a moderate cautery with an olive-oil soaked sponge; and make two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, a little below the hairline; and be careful not to cover the artery. of hair that pricks the eye Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and cauteries are made according to two methods: namely by fire or by heating medicine.
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
When they (hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in your care; afterward, on a piece of paper place an outline that is similar to the leaf of a fern, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered lichen of parsley on the eye, then heat the cautery of the shape that is shown here:
After cauterizing along the outline that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burned in that spot; and the sign of the success of the operation is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs standing up at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like that for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on until the burn is healed; after that, treat with ointment until it is healed.
And if after that the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then repeat the cautery on the same spot as before; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, and is even, and do not prick the eye with the hairs.
The fiery cautery of medicine is what you should instruct the patient to do: let the hairs grow long and even, then make a parchment in the shape of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool down, then spread it on the form that you have made similar to the fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in only one eye, then work on one side, and if it is on both sides as well; and place cotton soaked in egg yolk under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your care and place your hand over the medicine, and press a little and move it every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he will feel it like the biting of fire. When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from the wound. And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the wound's crust and check if you see the skin underneath lifted as if it was lifted by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is so, then it is good. If not, then apply more medicine on the wound until your work is even and your eyes are healed; then put a wet cotton swab with butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed; after that, cure the place of the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and other, until it is healed.
And if it is necessary for you to be very careful in your work so that the medicine does not fall into the eyes. And if the skin becomes soft and hairs prick into the eye, then reapply the medicine on the affected area where the skin has softened properly; after that cure it until it is healed; and this is the method of the mirthe leaf.[Note: The word "mirtre" in old French means a type of plant/herb. It's not clear which specific herb it refers to, but contextually it seems to be referring to some kind of medical dressing or herbal application used for healing.]
And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constraints (precautions); and let not the direct path be held as the same for one whose study is of this art.
of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the section on diseases, and your treatments do not help at all, then it is necessary that you perform cautery on them in this manner.
Instruct the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands so that it does not move or shift; then place a cotton swab soaked in egg white or pennyroyal juice on the eye; then heat the cautery which is parted: and attach it to the head like the shape of a dove's feather, with the tip touching the skin; if you wish, make it pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, also like a tent; but in any case, this which is attached is more useful for your work.
Afterwards press on the fistula if it is open, and extract the rottenness and dry matter from it; and if it is closed, then open it and extract the pus from it; afterwards place hot wheat flour on the cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part above the eye, so that your hand does not move foolishly; and place the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, it would be good. If not, then perform cautery again, and another time if you need to, and leave it for three days; afterwards place a cotton swab soaked in butter on it, and treat the wound with a drying ointment until it is healed; and if 40 days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and treat it according to what comes in its chapter.
And there is a type of cautery for a fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and open the place; after, put into the opening a thin piece of iron, the shape of which is as follows: And they make it the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the iron, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not enter his eye; and it is necessary to place cotton soaked in egg white or oil on the patient's eye: the lead will heal the fistula, and the healthy flesh will marvelously heal.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer a perforation to the nose and draw the fistula to the nose's flesh according to what is appropriate in its own place.

on an abscess of the throat
When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it has rotted and turned and become a fistula; and you treat it as we have mentioned in divisions, but it does not improve: then you must use a cautery appropriate to the size of the fistula; then put it over the opening or hole of the fistula, and keep your hand until the iron becomes hot and reaches the bottom of it and behind it; and do this once or twice, after treating as we have said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured this way, that is good; and if not, then you must uncover the area and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but it is of no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery so that its shape will be as follows: place a stick on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand in such a way that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cautery as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle for an hour.
And in this way the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is constricted, and the moisture is corrupted and dried up.
of toothache
When toothache comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical treatment is not effective, then it is necessary to use the cautery in two ways: with butter and fire.[IST] Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and moisten it in boiled butter, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this often until the virtue of it reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, which will form as follows, and place it on the tooth, holding your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be eased on the same day or the next. And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the form of the cautery:
When the scrofulous swellings are of phlegm and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the fire-iron until it is red-hot, and have two openings for the fumes to escape on the side away from the swelling; and place the hot iron on the abscess once or twice as needed, until you reach the bottom of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, place the iron accordingly, and leave it in place for three days; and apply a wet compress soaked in butter to ease the burn; after that, treat the area with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
When the moistures have overcome the channels of the peritoneum, and likewise when it is due to a cold complexion, then the patient should first be evacuated with soluble medicines; after that, perform cautery at the base of the throat, but make sure not to come too close to the throat, and only burn slightly. Then perform another cautery at the joint between the neck and the spine, using an iron shaped like a "clavile" as we have described before; and treat the area as we have said before until it is healed.

of the pleurisy cautery
The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your thumb; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little below in the area that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth and sixth ribs, inclining a little behind; and one cautery in the middle of the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two at the sides of the breast outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but instead act openly as if you are smelling something.
And certain ancients said that some people use a fire cautery similar to a razor, heating it and placing it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and then the pain goes away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is fear that the patient dies or a fistula develops which cannot be healed.

of dropsy

Afterwards, leave the cautery on to suppurate for a long time, and do not stop the patient's care after the cautery; and if healing is hastened, both intentions will be achieved with the help of God.

of the fleshiness called "thelul"
When you cut thelul (a term for fleshiness), heat up the cautery which resembles a razor, and then place it completely burning on the cut thelul; and leave your hand in that position until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein, from which the blood flows. Do this once or twice, and if there are many theluls, cauterize each one as we have said; after that cure them with beneficial ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on alchemy (possibly meaning a chemical substance), it will be of greater help.
of a wound poorly treated
When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will discuss in its place, then comes a disease that can only be cured by cautery.
When a fistula comes to someone and it is festering, casting off rotten and corrupt matter, you should test it with a thin probe and make sure that you know the depth of the entire probe. Afterwards, heat the cautery which resembles a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the length that the probe has entered, and continue heating the cautery until the rotten and corrupt flesh is burned away, once, or twice, or three times, depending on how much is needed. And be careful not to burn the nerves which are inside, and the large veins. If the fistula goes towards the body of the bladder and intestines, then be cautious of these areas, and do not perform this procedure outside of a fleshy area, and keep in mind that it is not safe; after caring for the area until it is healed, if the area becomes elevated and matter has been drained for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed. But if the matter is not drained, then know that the area is not fully healed, and the bone will become corrupted at its foundation. And so it is with one of those which we will discuss in its place.

of the pain in the hip. When pain comes to the hip's case, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated with what we have said in the division and the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with stinking pills or other good similar pills.
Afterward, perform cauterization; and the types of cauterization are according to two methods: that is, burning medicines, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many kinds, one of which is as follows: you cauterize on the boil's knob three triangular cauteries according to this form, and make a good depth and size, and let there be between each cautery a space the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on the top of the boil, so that there are four in this form:
And if you wish, cauterize it with the circular cautery that we have previously mentioned for the dislocation of the boil; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire boil, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
And this is the method used for sciatica, when the pain resides in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. And if it reaches the thigh and the leg, then two cauteries are made where the patient indicates the pain, and one above the ankle four fingers wide, slightly to the left; and let the cautery be knife-shaped, and let the fleshy areas be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize it in three or four points with the cautery called "points" where the patient feels the pain.
And if necessary, perform more cauterization; and if the patient feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then perform a knife-shaped or circular cautery, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long such that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause further harm and contraction to the patient.
And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and so did the foot, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. Afterwards, they died from a stomach ailment.
And if the pain is in two places together, perform cautery on both, in this manner. // And the wise men said in the cautery of inflammation, of which this is the method, make a such a iron and let it be as thick as a small bean stalk of date palm, or slightly less, and let there be crosspieces at equal distances, and let them be spaced as much apart as the width of a bean of pocktree; and let the crosspieces be turned in two parts, and let them be like knots, and there should be one well-made iron handle; and this is its shape.
And heat it until it is completely red and starts to drip, then place it on the swollen boil of the patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery rod and leave it for three days; then apply a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the treatment of ointment until it is healed.

of the back pain

of joint pain
When joint pain is due to humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when pain comes in the feet, which is properly called "gout" by laymen, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured by medicines, it can be cured by cauteries in the following way: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped in this form:
And if it is necessary to apply the cautery to the sole of the foot, let it be a whole cautery that is called "point". And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, which happens frequently, let three or four cauteries be made on each knee on every side, with the whole cautery olive-shaped; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand away for too long that the thickness of the flesh is not burnt.
And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the knuckles, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the wrists or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care to the patient and give them medicine. For if you provide good care and purge phlegm, they will heal with the help of God.
Of the opening of the abscess.
When the abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the haunches and this is recent, then when you see it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that evacuate the belly, so that feces descends from their stomach; after make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has subsided, and then massage it with your fingers, and apply a bandage below the abscess over the bone of the wrist, and in such a way that it forms half a circle above the body; then heat the cautery with which this form is made:
until it is white and releases pus. And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. of old pain in some member (limb) When pain comes to some member (limb), either from falling or being struck, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is of no use, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the "pointed" cautery, and let the cautery be according to the length of the member, its smallness, weakness, and strength, and its location, considering the twisting and pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that's good; if not, begin again with another cautery on top of it, for it is often the case that it must change to the member that is near it, so you must perform the cauteries until the patient is healed.
of leprosy (Hansen's disease)
Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, as well as diseases that come from the putrefaction of fluids and melancholy. When you see them to be cauterized, take care if the disease is at its beginning, and if it is treated according to what we have said in the division, and it does not worsen nor remain, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient's body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one on the crown of the head, and another towards the forehead at the end of the hair; and two on the two horns (temples), and one behind on the nape; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize the area according to what it is before.
And if the illness is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and six cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are at the back pressing down, so as not to burn them; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and one other on the bone of the stomach, and one other on the liver.
And know that when you make more cauteries, you do more help and benefit the patient; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because their body is already completely corrupted. And you should make the cauteries large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the ways of ironwork. Afterwards cure the wound with a mixture of flour of chickpeas with honey and other remedies until it is healed.

When the disease called "albaras" has become persistent and the means of medicine are of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a little deep, according to the quantity of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with bran of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and each one part of swallows' blood and sparrows' blood; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and expose it to air until it is healed.
The phrase "li cure de chancre par cautere" can be translated as "the treatment of chancre by cautery". Chancre was a term used in medieval medicine to refer to various types of ulcers or sores, including those associated with syphilis. Cautery was one method of treating these sores, and involved using a hot iron or other heated instrument to burn the affected area. This was believed to promote healing by destroying infected tissue and sealing off blood vessels. The specific instructions for performing such a treatment would depend on the particular medical text and context in which it appears.
When a chancre begins and you want to stop it, cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet, wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, using the "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
of the swelling that cannot heal
If someone has a disease called “adubelati” which does not heal, either due to the excess it causes, or due to the patient's old age and weakened condition (when they are very old and have little blood), or due to time; and you want to hasten its healing: then cauterize around it with many small cauteries in punctures. Afterward, leave it that way. Because it will hasten to heal.
And if you want to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery like this:
And place your hand in the middle of the ailment called "adubelati" until the cautery has pierced through to the heart, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them from outside in a manner that lightens the course of the gangrene. Afterward heal it until it is perfectly healed.
the healing by fire with iron
There is another kind of illness called "corrodens," which is nothing but an eating away of the limbs, just as fire consumes dry wood. If you see this disease in a place where it can tolerate cautery along with fire, then heat the iron cauteries very gently, both large and small, according to what is required for the location where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing remain of it. Then leave it alone for three days, and put soft bread soaked in oil on the heated cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, along with all of the corruption. Afterward heal with ointments that generate flesh. And if you see after three days that healthy flesh is not born, this is good; but if not, then repeat the cautery on the parts that remain corrupted. And sometimes this eating away has been cured by medicinal treatment instead of fire cautery; however, cautery with fire is of greater help. I have already mentioned the cure for the medical treatment in the division: take it when you need it.
of the splinters that come to (or go into) the feet
Often happens that at the feet arises a sickness called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large abscess that wounds the foot. And the cauteries for this sickness are of two kinds. That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery. The fire cautery is that you heat a small knife as big as a roof tile's pen, and make it from good iron, of a size that can reach the nail from all sides, and have fine edges; then place it very hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the base of the nail; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then make a plaster with crushed mallow leaves with oil, and leave the plaster on all night, and the nail will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with ointment spreading out the flesh until it is healed.
And if they are turned away from the body, both in hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this manner: take a rod of iron or copper, or a roof tile's pen, and place it on the nail and the althelul, that is to say porrelz verrues; and place the rod on it so that it boils all around, then put some hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning so that the edges of the rod come to the base of the nail, and can find a deep path through the hot water to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will be uprooted along with all its roots. Do so on each one, until you reach all that are on the body, then cure them with ointments that produce flesh.
The treatment for shaking/trembling.
When someone shakes from cold nerves or quartan fever or other causes, then you should apply four or five cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between each vertebra; and one cautery on the hip, and one on the stomach at the location of the olive cautery; this will stop the shaking, and hasten the healing of the cold disease.
of stinking pustules
Sometimes appear on the body, due to a lack of care, bad-smelling pustules which come from large corrupted matter. At first, when they appear, one should make a cautery on each head of the pustule: a subtle cautery made from a myrtle stick, with its tip taken by fire, or from a long aristolochia root, or from a round cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning, in this manner, and they cannot grow any further, but the superfluities from which they come are broken and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
when an artery is cut[The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries. It often happens that there is a large loss of blood from the artery which has been cut in a wound or incision of an abscess or in the cauterization of a limb, and similar things; and it is very difficult to stop the bleeding.
And yet, when this happens to someone, hasten to place your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press it very hard so that the blood is calmed beneath your finger, and no more comes out; then put
And if it jumps out when you remove your finger from above the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, quickly take another one of the cauteries that are in the fire.
And do not cease to do this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other harm comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is by one of the four ways that we have said: either by cautery, or by extraction when it is not treated, or by tightly binding with a bandage, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop blood; and let it be bound and held firmly.
Who will administer the stopping of the bleeding by tightly binding with bandages or by placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help then it is of no use.[Note: This sentence is a continuation of the previous translation and provides a cautionary statement about the methods mentioned in the previous sentence.]
And if it happens to someone who does not have medical equipment or medicine present, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and pull hard until it stays above the wound and vein; and he should not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood is congealed and thickened and stopped; and make preparations for what he needs in terms of cauteries and medicines.
We have told you in the first chapter all diseases in which it is necessary to use fire cautery or heated medicine, and we have described their causes, instruments, and forms; and I put this chapter about the head down to the feet, and I will go in this chapter the same way so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
And so as I begin this one, it is important, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first chapter on cauteries, and therefore greater caution is required.
For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
And I warn you not to undertake folly. For many kinds of people come to cures: those who are so afflicted by their illness that they easily die due to the severity they find in their disease, and the gravity of its malice; and one should fear these. And among them are those who give you their trust and say: "wait, I am healed." The illness is scornful. It is not at all appropriate to agree with those who come to you with this attitude, but rather put more effort into your honor than your greed, and do not foolishly open up for those about whom you are uncertain and can potentially harm your reputation; and use prognostication and indication in the care of your patients so that their health may be restored; and this will help you to achieve good renown, glory, and praise.
Dear son, may Our Lord grant you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inhale the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.

"the head full of water" or "the swollen head"
"Know that this disease often occurs in children during childbirth, and when the birth is difficult and the mother grips the child's head too hard; and sometimes it happens for no apparent reason."
"And I have never seen this disease except in children, and among those that I have seen, their deaths came quickly; and for this reason it seems better to me to leave such work to more skilled practitioners."
"And I saw a child whose head was full of water and became larger every day until it could no longer support its own weight; and the fluid increased so much that he died, and this fluid collects under the bone at the temple, between the brain and the skull; and the procedure is such when the fluid is between the brain and the bone, and the abscess is small, that you make an incision in the head, a slit wide enough for the fluid to flow out; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the fluid can escape; and here is the shape of the spatula:"

And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs you see are that the corners of the mouth are open on both sides, and pus comes out when you press it from the inside with your hand, and this does not respond (to treatment); then you must make three incisions in the middle of the chin, following this pattern:
After the incision, remove all the pus. Then bind the incisions with cloth and powder, and apply wine and oil. Leave it like this until the fifth day; then unbind it, and treat the wound with bandages and ointments. Also continue to keep the chin bound up, and give the patient dry food with little moisture until the limb is healed and healthy again.
And another method of incision is to observe where the swelling of the abscess is most prominent, and where the pus has gathered; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Cut then at the place where the abscess is open, and the filling of water, and the opening according to what you have the power; and take care not to cut the artery; and if blood flows, so that the patient dies from the outpouring of blood and evacuation of moisture.

When old-age migraine comes, and acute catarrh, due to moisture in the tears and heat in the temples and swelling of the crazy ancient head and similar things, and it is treated by various medical cures but none bring improvement, then let us extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
And the manner of their extraction is that the patient shaves the hairs from their temples and pays attention to the artery that appears in the temple, for it appears clearly through its beating, and is not deeply hidden except in some men who are very cold; and if it is hidden, let the patient strain their neck with some cloths, then rub the area with a rough cloth and apply hot water to it until the artery is clearly visible; then take the spatula of the form described:
Then gently flay the skin until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with forceps and separate it well from the membranes beneath it on each side; and if the arteries are fine, turn them with the point of a hook, then cut that part according to the size of the two holes. For if it is not cut, the blood will not come out completely.
And draw blood from the six holes until three have been made; and if the arteries are large, you must tie them in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that rotting does not occur before the wound is healed and proper bleeding occurs; then cut away any excess tissue between the two ties at once; and if you wish, cauterize the wound with a knife-edged cautery to the bone until the holes are closed; this is the more effective method, if the patient does not have a fever and has a hot complexion.
For the cautery serves to end moisture: therefore it is of greater help for moisture-related conditions. Where it is necessary for the extraction of arteries, that one fills the wound with old cotton and places well-made bandages on top; and when they are loosened, they should be cared for with dry medicines that cause flesh to grow, and with bandages, until it is healed; and if blood flows from the slit of the artery as much as you work, then hurry to cover it with a hot cautery, or fill the wound with vitriol and hold it with your hand until the blood stops; and if you don't have this present, then place your finger on the wound until the blood clots, and pour cold water over the wound until it ceases, and hold it as is necessary; and that which is easier and lighter in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the slit with this two-part cutting cautery, but let the cuts be thick to keep their heat longer. For when the instrument is too thin, it holds its heat less. And there should be a finger's breadth of space between the two knives, and then when you have marked the two places, place the red-hot iron on them until it reaches the bone, and cut the slit in two places; and they should be far apart because this cutting cautery is not welded together in its entirety; and that is the form of the cautery.
tears

on ear stoppage.
All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains or small animals, stone from mines or similar things such as iron; seed such as lice, beans, peas; or fluid such as water and earwax and similar things.
When it falls into the ear a stone or other object that does not fit in the ear nor grows in the ear, place the ear towards the sun. If you see the stone, drip a few drops of violet oil or sesame oil, then attempt extraction; and make them sneeze using some condiment, and stop up their nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and stretch the ear upwards. This cure often works; and if it does not work, attempt extraction using fine pincers, of which this is the method:
If it comes out with the pincers, that is good. If not, attempt extraction using a fine hook made of thin wire; and if it does not come out this way either, make a small tube of tin and insert the end of the tube into the ear hole, stopping up what is around the tube with soft wax so that air cannot enter with the tube; then pull it out strongly, as it often comes out in this way. And if it does not come out in this manner, take birdlime with which birds are caught, and put some on an instrument made for this purpose, and place a piece of cotton around; then press the birdlime onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull it out. And if it does not come out with all of the things we have mentioned, then quickly proceed to lancing the ear so that abscess and swelling do not occur. The method of lancing is as follows: first bleed the patient from the head, draining blood according to their strength, then have the patient sit between your hands with their ear facing upwards; make a small incision at the base of the ear in the fatty area, and let the incision be shaped like a crescent moon until you reach the stone, then remove it as well as you can and quickly suck on it with your mouth; continue this treatment until it is healed. and make an incision on that swelling. But do not do so when you think that the swelling is moist due to ear moisture, until you have made many pieces of it; then extract it with delicate forceps and suction, as we have said, so that the extraction is eased.
Therefore, in the water that falls in the ear, the patient should use sneezing with previous conditions, and fill the ear with wadding of old cotton. And lie on that same ear where the water is. If it comes out by this, it's good. If not, take many small and light pebbles, and heat them a little in the fire; and put one of these stones in the patient's ear, and jump on the other side, and strike another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this stone by stone until all the water comes out, and thus it will all come out; and if you see, take a reed, and put one end in the ear, and light the other end with fire until the larger reed is burnt; then do the same thing again with another reed until all the water comes out, as we have said with the stone.
In the extraction of the creature, if it is of small size, such as a louse and similar things, cure it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that can be felt, then prepare for the extraction with forceps; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.

of ear stoppings
No child is born who does not have some hole in the ears; and this same thing happens to adults through blocking of wounds or pus inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes come from deep within the ear so that they cannot be seen; and sometimes there is a small sac below the opening of the ear, and one can see it well.
Then the one that comes deep, if one cannot see it, is of difficult healing in many ways; and in the one that can be seen, it is necessary for you to put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the apparation of pus, then work on it all this time span with which this procedure is formed:
And let it be sharp and piercing both in front and behind, so that it does not wound the ear; if the pus is in the flesh or core of the ear, then hold it with delicate pincers, and cut it lightly, until all the flesh is removed.
And if the pus is deep in the ear, then take a delicate lancet, heat it slightly by the fire, and place it in the core of the ear. If you feel the pus from which the patient feels discomfort in hearing, pierce it lightly, and make sure not to injure the nerves of the ear; then insert into the ear a wick according to the width of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Do this for several days until the wound is healed, or take a wick and moisten it in rose water, and powder on top with crushed vitriol; and if you see swelling in the ear, then it is necessary to remove the wick and replace it with another one moistened in cerote made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then continue to treat it until it is healed.
And if bleeding occurs, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, place it on the ear, and use other cures that stop bleeding as described in the treatment of distillations.

Many times there come from the eyelids small things that seem gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this, this illness is called "hail", and it is a gathering of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the treatment is as follows: take heed if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is an easy thing to know; then make an incision of appropriate size, then gently scrape from each part, then take with tweezers and cut. of the eyelid fat
Exinach is a fat that accumulates in the paper of the eyelids, and this happens more often in children than in others, and it bothers their eyes very much, and they get catarrh in the mornings, and they cannot look at the sunlight because their tears rush to their eyes; and because of this, they often lie on their faces and sleep, and their eyelids under their eyebrows are moist and swollen, and the appearance is covered by the exinach that appears in the eye. And when you press the place with your fingers, you can feel the exinach between them.
And the manner of the work is that the patient places his head on your safe place; and then take a linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains pus from each part, then put it on top of it; and press with your hands on one side and the other, so that the pus is gathered within the circle; then make in the middle of the moisturized area with a sharp-pointed spatula an incision of a width, and let it not be any larger than the wound that is made when opening a vein; and make the skin go deep until you reach the pus; and in several ways, the pus comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Then pull out completely a piece of cloth between your fingers away from the incision, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread; and make sure that you do not press on the incision, that you do not come to the whole spatula up to the eye, that you do not wound it.
And if the pus does not come out at the beginning of the incision, then slightly increase the incision a little bit until it appears; then extract it as we have said, then wet cloths with vinegar and water, and put them on top, and apply bandages.
And if there are such people who grind salt and put it on to corrupt the moisture that remains. Then cure it until it is healed. And if an abscess comes to the place, then cure it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
of the hairs of the genital area
When hairs grow on the genital area other than naturally and are neglected, they harm the eyes and bring about various illnesses such as excessive tearing and softening of the papillae and inflammation, to the point of destroying the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: either through cauterization with fire, or through medicine as described in the chapter on cauterization, and this is done through incision and suturing or through caustics, depending on what I will say.
You should place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the affected eye towards your left hand; if it is turned, that is good; if not, put a needle with one thread through it; and let this be next to the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow from among these hairs, and pull one thread over the entire eyelid, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision beneath the eyelid, beneath the extra hairs, reaching all the way to the spatula, from the large tear duct to the small one; then remove one thread, and place underneath the eyelid a small cotton and linen tent, then apply to the eyelid a figure of an eye shape, such as a myrtle leaf, and in any case it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you intend to raise the eyelid which is determined.[translated by me so I can't guarantee accuracy]

The treatment of veins is as follows: and it is that you fold the paper and make a hole in it according to what I have said, and then make two incisions with skill, and two thin ligatures as long as the paper and as wide as the width of the spatula; and cut the two ends of the two parts where you hold the threads; then carefully bring the one and the other together on top of the paper, and tightly tie the two ligatures from the two parts; and leave it like this for several days, and the skin that was constricted will die, become hard and rot, so that it falls off by itself.

of the decay/wasting away of the eye
When this disease called "aleacrati" or decay comes to the eye, it can happen in two ways: one natural and the other unnatural. And it happens suddenly due to a wound, or by a surgeon's knife or cautery, and similar things.
And the method of treatment for this is that you split open the scar tissue, separate its lips, and put linen bandages inside, keeping it in place until it has healed; and one must not use drying or constricting substances in its care. For if you do so, the illness will return worse than before. Instead, use softening substances, such as fenugreek. And cook barley water or aloe and linseed, and apply warm oil infused with diluted rose oil, and wrap it with a bandage.
And the key to your treatment is to be careful that it does not heal in the same shape as before; and these methods we have mentioned are only adjustments for this disease, so that it does not return to its previous state.
of flesh coming in the eye (Flesh growth in the eye)
This illness that is truly called "axacrati," and is natural and accidental. The accident comes from wound and cracking and cauterization and similar things; and the way of the work in it is that you take a needle, in which there is a double thread, and stick it in the flesh, and make it pass from the left tear duct to the right, so that the threads come out in two parts of the flesh; then stretch the flesh above over the entire needle, and bind it with a spatula wide.
And if the paper's shape returns as it should, that is good; if not, take a razor and place it in the crack, and turn the paper, and make two cracks or cuts inside the paper; and let the ends of the two cracks be at the two angles of the incision that you have made, and make them into a shape so that when they are assembled, it looks like the figure of a letter called "J"; then remove the flesh, according to how much its sides are under the paper, then join the two separated parts, and sew them with a thread of wool; then cure it with the medicines we have mentioned, such as softening agents, and bandages, until it is healed.
And if the illness comes from cracking or stitching or cauterization, it is necessary to make a clean cut in the paper along the hairs of the crack, and according to what is said before; then separate between the two books of a bandage as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the illness, for it is very diverse in shape, and wise masters should prepare all their power to make it return to its natural shape; and the patient himself, depending on what work and instruments are needed, should be placed in several positions.
quickly of the paper
When this bonding occurs in men in such a way that the paper on top is glued to the white of the eye, and it cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you should insert the tip of a razor underneath the paper and lift it up; and stretch it with forceps, so as to cut what adheres to the thin membrane, which should not be too sharp or too cutting, so that the patient cannot endure the sharp membrane scraping their eye; and let your incision, when you flay this assembly, be light, so that the paper may return to its natural shape; and let the entire assembly be healed, and sometimes use salty water, and sweet water, and collyrium (eye medication); then place a linen tent between the paper and the eye, and put damp wool on the eye with an abundance of egg; and after three days, use collyrium and other wound-healing substances until it is healed.
of the eyelid.
Know that the eyelid is of two kinds: one is fleshy and similar to a hard zit, and another which is not fleshy but rather looks like congealed white mucus, which when touched with iron and tried to be grasped with forceps, cannot be; and both forms begin near the outer corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eyeball and all light and movement of the eye.
And the manner of the incision is as follows: the patient should place their head in your lap, then you open their eyes. Lift the paper (eyelid) with your hand and pull the eyelashes with forceps, stretching it out; then take a needle and put in it a horsehair or cow hair and strong thread; double the tip of the needle a little bit and insert it into the eyelid, passing it all the way through and stitching the eyelid with a thread, stretching it out, and flay it (remove the skin) from the edge of the eyelid that follows the eyeball and the lashes to the hairline, then cut the remaining part at the root near the outer corner of the eye as thinly as possible with small forceps. Leave the flesh on the eyeball or eyelid so that the normal flow of tears is not blocked by the incision; sometimes the eyelid heals only at the edge and stitches, just as we said before; then you remove the skin in this manner:
And be careful that the retractor does not touch the fleshy towel and break it, and that the iris is not pierced; and after the incision, put a little bit of crushed clay into the eye, and a collyrium made of litharge, and leave it until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
And if the nail is not sensitive and you cannot insert the needle, and the forceps cannot enter, this type of nail is often cured with medicines; and it grows back as I have mentioned in the division, and if you see it covered, have the patient's eye worked on, and take the retractor that is slightly pointed according to this form:
And carefully cut the nail above, and if you see that it is not thinning and the flesh is closing in, distill into the eye from your mouth a collyrium made of litharge and red clay, and stop up the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same procedure, until it is completely removed.
If there is nothing contrary in the eye, such as a hot abscess, then leave it alone and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid hinders the eye with great harm, then suspend it at the corner and cut off a part of it and not all, so that tears do not come to it; then distill red collyrium into the eye which is made of lithargyre.

And sometimes the eyelids of certain men are born with red flesh that covers the pupil, turns upwards and inward, and appears like a baluster rose; and the operation consists of having the patient place their head over you, then opening their eyes, and pulling all that red flesh towards the eyebrow hairs using tweezers and holding it tightly; then cutting the first layer of flesh with a razor until the end, while taking care not to wound the eye during the procedure; and let the incision of the scalpel be as we have said in the incision of the nail and the small nerves from which one removes the skin, as the form after this chapter shows.
And when the incision is completed and all the flesh has been removed, then apply oil of crushed eggshell or distill red collyrium and similar corrosive medicines to the eye; place cotton with egg white over the eye so that it is protected from hot abscess; and if anything remains, and the pus rises, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave the eye and treat the abscess with calming agents; then return to your work once it has healed, and do this each time flesh grows in the eye by this method.

There are red veins that are located on the eye and take away from the eyes' function, weakening it all day long. of the eye fistula.
The physicians call this type of fistula "arissati": when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a trick to cut open the abscess where it should burst, and draw out all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, take all the instruments described in this form; and it is called "rough surface", and make it with a hot iron in the shape of a narrow chief reont, and point it like a file as shown in the present form:
And place the leg (literally: "the level" or "side") of the corrupted bone on top, then turn it between your hands and press your hand slightly until you know that the corruption is reset; and do this several times, then restore the leg with drying medicines.
If the level is united and flesh grows, and the flesh of the wound is united, and it remains so for 40 days without becoming inflamed or infected, then know that it is healed. If not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the nose according to this form: that you expose the bone a second time with iron, and with humid medicines, and when it has been exposed, take a gimlet in this shape, and let the head of the iron be trident-shaped, and the rod be tapered up to the tip as you see here:
Then place it (the gimlet) next to the bone near the tear duct, and move your hand away from the eye a little bit, then turn the whole gimlet until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through this sensation: if they hold their hand over their nose, they will notice the wind leaving. Once this is done, restore the level with dry medicines as I have taught you. And when the flesh grows back and hardens, the matter (pus) goes to the nose; this is easier for the patient.
of the eye socket/orbit dislocation
When the eye is open wide all around and there is no obstruction or reduction in size, then you should bind the patient; next, cleanse, then apply leeches or cupping glasses without causing harm to heal, then place a mixture of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocola on the eye; then bandage it and cover it with cloths and bandages; and make sure the cloths are quite soft, and fold each one in four layers, and apply them gradually according to the size of the eye; then bandage it tightly with a firm piece of cloth, and reapply the cupping glasses without causing harm; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye bandaged both day and night, and if the band becomes loose, tighten it considerably; then remove the band after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, reapply the poultice, cloths, band, and cupping glasses until it heals.
of a detached retina.
When there is a disruption in the retina and it becomes visible, appearing like a grain of resin and frightening to see; then if you see such a thing, the treatment is as follows: insert a needle into the root of the affected part from below all the way up to above, then insert another needle with a double thread in the outer corner; and make it perforate, leaving the first needle according to its position; then cut off the excess thread from the needle and tie one end of the uvea, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a wet linen on the eye; leave it until the thread dries with the uvea, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound heals; sometimes the wound is constricted by the uvea on both sides of a circle of cloth until it heals.
And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from within the eye, and let the watery humor come out, and let the eye fall down and sink in; then pull it out until it is healed.
Of the swelling of the eye.
This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but swelling that has gathered in the eye, appearing as water descending, and it is not actually water; and the manner of its appearance is such that you make the patient sit on a well-prepared and straight seat, then take their head with both hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it be pierced and if the light does not fall down and become dimmed, and the patient can see things as usual, and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said, make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and insert it through the cornea, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the crown, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, let warm distilled water mixed with honey be instilled into the eye, or water or fenugreek boiled with honey, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed.
of the waters (or fluids) of the eye.
We have similarities of waters in the division, and that which is necessary to pierce; and one must work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and tie the healthy eye very tightly; then put the paper on the eye in your left hand if the eye is left, or in your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the size of a grain in that whorl of the eye on the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument called "almagda" forcefully and turn your hand until it pierces in the whorl of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the grain to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it down under one way after another. If the water comes out now, let the patient look at what is before him and the instrument in his eye.
After a short rest, and if the water rises again along the second way, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and it no longer rises, then gently remove almagda by turning your hand a little at a time; and then put in a little bit of gemstone saltwater, and lift the eye inside. Then place over the eye cotton or damp wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg yolk, and bind it with the healthy eye.
