of the flesh near the nose
Sometimes different kinds of fleshy growths appear near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such growths that have a swollen part of a foxy color, and also soft flesh of bone color. In the case of this kind of growth that is soft, but not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands with their face towards the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the instrument to those growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp, fine spatula on one side, until you are certain that the growth is completely removed.
And if any part remains that cannot be cut, you should open it with all the very fine and light instruments, leaving nothing behind; and if pus forms, or an abscess arises, treat it as necessary; and if they are harmful abscesses, hurry and cauterize until the blood stops flowing and all growths are removed, then pour wine or vinegar on the nose.
If the nose becomes blocked and moisture reaches the palate, this means it is healed; but if the moisture does not drain as it should, this indicates that there is growth in the bone above which the instruments cannot reach. In this case, you should insert a fairly thick linen thread with evenly spaced knots about the width of a fingernail or less. Place the patient's head over the thread and draw it gently up into the nose until it emerges from the nostril in the mouth; children often do this in school, and it is an easy thing to do. Hold the emerging end of the thread that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots until you know which ones have become embedded in the flesh. Then pull the thread, wipe away any blood, moisten it with Egyptian ointment, and replace it in the nose as before. Repeat this process for three days or more, until all remaining growth has been dissolved by the ointment. Then place a piece of wax in the nostril for several days until the area is healed; if drying medicines are required, use them. This is the method for clearing blockages in the nose using an instrument that distills oil and medicine into the nose.[ITA] Ecco la traduzione linea per linea del testo:

of flesh from the nose
Often, a disease arises in the head of the nose, called "telul," which grows and becomes large to the point that it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it completely, then place the cautery or hot medicine on it; and if it is delayed until it has grown large, be careful if it is hard, of a dark color, and with little sensation: do not touch it at all with iron because it is an inflamed abscess, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of a dark color, and you see that it can be completely cut, then empty the patient's nose and cut it carefully without fear, and cure the place with drying and constricting things.
when the nose is cut and sewn.
Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must cauterize all the edges of them until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture, and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood, and crushed incense; and place powders on top of a piece of strong plaster or another adhesive plaster, and leave it until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.

of abscesses of the lips
To some men there come within the lips hard abscesses, similar to grains of pepper, sometimes smaller and sometimes larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut in each part; then apply the place after the incision of powdered vitriol until the blood is stopped; and then clean the wound with dry things until it heals.
of the flesh of the gums
Often, a swelling of the flesh of the gums arises, which the ancients called "albulus"; then you should hold it with tongs and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood run out; then put vitriol powder or other drying and constricting powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, then cut it again and cauterize it: for it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments for cutting.

Sometimes, accumulations occur on the top of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth become black, greenish, and gray, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you should have the patient sit between your hands, and their chin in your holy hand, and clean the visible teeth or the scabs until nothing remains; and similarly for the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other stains, until they are cleaned; and if you remove what is there at the first cleaning, it is good; if not, then resume again on the second day and the third, until everything is cleaned; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments for cleaning, depending on what the task requires, because the scrapers used to clean above the teeth have different forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared.
It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as much as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very risky substance up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it. Then, when the patient is ready to have it pulled, you must make sure that you identify the problematic tooth. Often, the pain deceives the patient, and they think the issue is in a healthy tooth, leading them to have a good tooth extracted; however, the pain does not subside because of this, as we have already seen done by some ignorant surgeons. Once you are certain of the problematic tooth, you must cauterize all around it with a strong spatula to protect the gum from all sides. Then, place the molar between your fingers or use fine-tipped pliers and gently pull at the root until it is loosened. Make sure to securely fasten the pliers, and have the patient sit between your knees so that they cannot move during the procedure.
After extracting the tooth carefully without breaking it, if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently insert it on both sides to loosen it further, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is cracked or decayed, you must fill it with cloth where the cracks are, then gently squeeze it with pliers so that it doesn't break. It's important to work very delicately around the gum to widen the socket and remove any remaining fragments of the tooth.
I advise you to be careful not to break the tooth and leave a piece in the patient's mouth, as this could result in even greater pain than before due to the malice of the root. Also, be cautious not to act like ignorant surgeons who, out of haste and arrogance, sometimes break the jaw and do not address the issue at all; instead, they cause significant illness due to the remaining roots or broken jaw, as we have often seen. After extracting the tooth, rinse the area with wine, vinegar, or saltwater, especially if bleeding occurs, which is common. If that doesn't help, use vitriol and if it still persists, cauterize the wound.

when the tooth loosens.
When the teeth loosen, either from a blow or falling, and the patient cannot bite down on what they eat without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines but to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose ones between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more than one, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again up to the point where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the loose teeth with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose one, so that it does not wound the tongue; and then leave it as tight as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, constrict it again with another wire; and let it remain and serve in this way all its time, and this is the method for aligning two healthy teeth and two loose ones, as you see.
And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place as soon as possible, as we have said; and let no one who is not wise and skilled meddle with it; and sometimes the form of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the empty socket, and it is constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
to cut the tie of the tongue.
Sometimes there is a ligament beneath the tongue, which is natural at birth or due to an accidental wound that has healed; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hand, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its attachment. If there is hardness or knots, which is due to a hasty wound healing, insert the unicorn (a surgical instrument) and widen the ligament; and be careful not to make the incision too deep, as the artery beneath could be damaged. Then apply a compress of rose water and vinegar or cold water, then place a linen bandage under the tongue. Have the patient wear it every night so that the wound does not heal. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder; and if the bleeding persists, cauterize it with a ligature cautery which is good for this purpose; then continue treatment until it heals.[STHAPDA: This text describes a surgical procedure for releasing a tongue-tie (ankyloglossia). It advises to cut the lingual frenulum, the membrane connecting the underside of the tongue to the floor of the mouth. If there are hard knots or adhesions due to previous wound healing, it recommends using a surgical instrument such as an unicorn (a type of forceps) to widen the ligament and cut it with caution to avoid damaging the artery beneath. After the procedure, a linen bandage is placed under the tongue, which should be worn every night until healing occurs. The text also advises on how to manage bleeding if it occurs.]

of abscesses in the throat

And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and it had completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not exhale due to the passage that was stopped up, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had stayed like that for one day or two. And the abscess was so swollen that it had already pushed out two pieces through the two nostrils. I hurried then, and inserted a probe into one of them, then pulled it out and extracted a large amount of pus; then I did the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; after that, I inserted the probe into these abscesses, and cut off a part of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she started to drink water and then wine, and I kept cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess increased again, and filled the space that I had emptied, so that it became very large; then I squeezed it and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it did not increase anymore; and I left that place, and I do not know what God did with her after me.
of the eye.
When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below thick and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is fine, then you must make an incision; and the one that is rounded together and is not long; and it is blood-red or ash-colored or black, then you must avoid making an incision near it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit in front of the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye, and pull it down, and make an incision with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And you should not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice, and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then you must use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the manner of cautery is lukewarm. This treatment is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elder and similar herbs, and gather them all or some of them in one pot, and put them in a pot and boil; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot have an instrument like this: And whether it be of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes be put in the patient's mouth until the steam reaches the eye through the canal, until the eye is made lifeless; then begin to frequently replace it, until the eye dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the onset of a hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it unless at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and place an eggshell within the patient's head, so that the patient's mouth does not become too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the steam to harm the mouth, and it is a good remedy together with being healthy.
Often a bone or a fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat; therefore, you must pull out what you can see, and press down on the patient's tongue with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what you cannot see and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit, so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of napkin, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a string to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell up, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out through what we have said, take an instrument made of reed in this form:

The chapter on abscesses.
Many similarities of abscess are, according to what the following remembrance brings in this book, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own likeness, and those that hold moisture. And the second way is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different than those of the bottom, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one should have its judgment in the work.
And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is mature according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is entirely corrupted, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is mature, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the bottom, so one should pierce it as soon as it is mature; and one must not pierce a grown abscess without completed digestion, except for those that are near the bottom, lest it corrupts in depth, and becomes elongated, and causes a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the hour of the piercing of the abscess when it is mature according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the lessening of the fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and the swelling and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the place where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it appears to move; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and in all places where there are no folds.
And in those that fold, according to the member. And when the abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it is strengthened after completed digestion, as we have said. For if you pierce it before this, the body of the pus will be elongated and full of much filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And some abscesses must be pierced according to the width of the body, according to what is necessary for the member. And one must make small incisions in small abscesses, and large incisions in large ones, and many cuts according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses that require removing the core and covering it; when it has become as a piece of cloth, and is dead, one must do as with boils: and some abscesses are cut in three angles, and some are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of glands; and there are those that have a round cut, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Those who have no visible abscess, such as a mild subcutaneous one, should be fully lanced. And when the abscess is large, and has collected a great deal of pus, you should not remove all of it at once when you lance it, but instead remove some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and remove some more; do this repeatedly, gradually increasing the amount removed each time, until all of the pus has drained out. The same procedure should be followed for those of weak constitution, women, young children, or frail old men. This is because the spirit may suddenly leap with the release of pus, which could potentially cause the death of the patient. Therefore, exercise great caution in this matter, and once you have lanced the abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small. If it is a simple cut, then apply soft bandages made of linen or old cotton. But if it is a large abscess with many openings, then insert a tent into each one so that they press against each other. And if you have removed a piece of skin from the abscess and turned it back, then fill the hole with soft cotton or linen rags without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and continue to treat the wound with ointment until it has healed.
And if bleeding occurs during your procedure, apply cold water and a compress to the area repeatedly. And if the bleeding persists, provide treatment and care, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book. And if it is during the winter months, and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, then place tents and wet cloths soaked in warm wine and oil on top of it. And if it is during the summer, and the area is fleshy, then apply damp cloths soaked in water and oil or warm wine and oil for three days, as we have said; and then unbind the abscess, dry and clean it, and treat it until it has healed.
And this is what should be universally understood in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one must proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here begins that chapter.[1](#myfootnote1)

In this remedy, I have never seen anyone who dared to perform the cure with iron.
And the ancients said that it is made in such a way as the branch which is entwined around the vine, in such a manner that you bind the vessels, after the cut on top of them lightly underneath.
Then cut in half and cure the abscess of those who work on it, until the vessels burst; and cure it as we have said, until it is healed.
Sometimes there comes rupture in the haunches, as we have said, and the place is open; and none of the intestines descend to the hips, and if any do descend, it is little, and it heals every hour.

And the treatment is by cauterization, as we have previously said; and it can be cured by iron in this manner:
And the patient lies face down on their back between your hands, then cut the swollen area of the wound to a width of about three fingers' breadth;[ ]{.break}

of the softening of the skin of the buttocks.
The skin of the buttocks is often softened in some men because the fat within is softened and it is visible. And when one wants to heal it, it is necessary for the patient to lie on their stomach, and cut the softened skin that is above the natural skin; then bring the two lips together with a stitch, and if you see, first sew the excess softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and heal it like other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the threads.
of the surgery/treatment
Know that surgery is condemned in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; however, there are two reasons why it is necessary: one is that the physician must be able to respond when asked about it and know how to perform it; and the second is that we often need to surgically treat animals for our own benefit, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts. I say then that surgery is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the case of surgery by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until its genitals become soft and relaxed; then, with your hand, pull them back into place until you feel no resistance.
Hermaphrodites
Hermaphrodites are of two types for men: one is that between the two genitals there is an appearance like the form of a woman's nature, with hair and sometimes urinating from it. And the other type is in women, with something resembling a penis and two genitals. The cure for both men and women is to cut off the attached parts and heal them as you would other wounds; but for the second type, for men whose urine comes out through the skin of the genitals, there is no cure.
of the tetanus (tension muscle stiffness)
Tetanus is a growth attached to the eyelid, which is too ugly to look at; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is its treatment. You should trim the excess of the tetanus with your hand or tweezers, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, to avoid bleeding, then cure another wound until it heals; and apply it to another flesh that arises at the mouth of the sore, and it may fall out, and it resembles a cow's udder, and for this reason, the ancients called it "cow disease". Therefore, you should cut it, as we have said about tetanus, and cure it until it heals.
of erratics (rocks or stones that have been moved or deposited by natural forces)
Erratics (infertility) is when the opening of the female's reproductive system is not fully open or is too small; and it can be natural at birth or caused by an accident due to illness, or by a growth, or a subtle or thick syphilis that has entered deep into the vagina, on the sides, underneath, or anywhere else; and this prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation. The knowledge of this is determined by the appearance of the hymen. If the stoppage is visible, then you should use your fingers or a probe. If it is a subtle syphilis and it is close to the two lips, then hurry and rotate it like this: place your two index fingers together and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread apart; then stretch the two lips widely apart so that the subtle syphilis can be reached and placed above the stoppage; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it on the opening, and have the woman lie with a man every day so that it does not close up. If the syphilis is hard and thick, then you must cut it like a leaf of myrtle. If the stoppage is made of flesh, then suspend it with tweezers and cut it; and use hemostatic medicines such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, mixed with egg yolk; then prepare a wide funnel made of wood, so that the wound does not close up; and treat it in this way for a long time and provide a tent made of dry linen; then cure other wounds until it heals. And when flesh grows in the vagina, it must be cut according to this method, except for deeply ingrown abscesses. For an ingrown abscess in the vagina, one should not touch it with fire.
of hemorrhoids
Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they become hardened and are called "teluel." We have mentioned their similarities, signs, and divisions in the previous section. I will now discuss those that can be cured. I say that both hemorrhoids and teluel, when deeply embedded in the rectum and not felt during defecation, cannot be treated by surgery. Those that are located at the opening of the rectum can be felt and are treatable. Therefore, it is necessary to place the woman in a cool house, then use tongs or forceps to pull on the teluel's roots, apply medicines that constrict blood flow such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and similar things; then elevate her legs against the wall for an hour, followed by immersion in cold water. If bleeding occurs, place her in a decoction of sumac, pomegranate bark, galls, and similar things, then prepare a bread poultice with barley flour, honey, and vinegar, and apply it to her back. If the bleeding stops, that is good. Otherwise, apply cups to her back and breasts without causing injury; then take wool, soak it in plantain or agrimony juice with old wine, and warm it up at the affected area. When the abscess subsides, treat the area with ointment until healed; and the one called "albathir" is red and resembles a rough surface, it needs to be treated in the same way as teluel, and then continue treatment until fully healed.
of abscesses in the anus
There are many types of abscesses that occur in the anus, such as chancre, phlegmonous abscess, herpes, eczema, fistula, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, among other conditions mentioned in the previous section. Therefore, it is necessary for me to discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the anus, which is not one of those treated with boil lancing. If you want to know about surgical treatment, observe if the abscess is hard at its onset, full of heat and fever, and becoming red if visible. Do not rush to make an incision, but wait until the pain subsides; then have the patient sit on a seat with two small cushions to lean on, place a support behind their back, raise their legs above the level of their thighs, separate their knees, and place their arms under their knees, tying them securely. Then administer an enema to soften the stool; insert the instrument used to open the anus (refer to the following form); and be careful when inserting it not to penetrate deeper than necessary, avoiding injury to the patient. If the instrument is too large, cover the area with cloths to prevent discomfort. Place the tip of the instrument against the abscess and hold it there until the pus flows out. Once the pus has drained, place moist swabs soaked in oil (rose or green virgin) inside the wound, deep within the anus; then cover the area with clean, damp wool soaked in water or marshmallow root decoction. After two days, treat the wound with appropriate ointment until it heals. Sometimes, perform an enema of warm water and honey, followed by a decoction of lily roots and aristolochia; then return to applying the ointment. If the wound is closed in the anus, be careful not to use hot iron, but treat it as we have mentioned in the division.
of childbirth
It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the shape of a natural childbirth and its signs, which are: when you see the woman pressing downwards and desiring to smell the armpit; then the baby hastens to come out; thus, know that this birth is according to nature, and the exit is under its head, and the afterbirth with it. And when you see these signs, you should gently press on her belly so that the baby comes out quickly, for once it rests on its head, the afterbirth will come out with it, and the woman will be relieved of her impurities through good purification. But if it comes out any other way, then it is not natural. For sometimes it comes out feet first, or outside the body, such as the hands or the legs, or it turns over on its belly, and perhaps even upside down; thus, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and skilled in these matters, and to be wary of error and deception. And I will show you all the shapes and how one should assist in each case.
If the baby comes out headfirst in a natural birth, and the woman is having a difficult time, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool or be held by other women. Anoint her privates with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then place the small spatula-shaped instrument (the form of which is shown below) between the midwife's fingers. and cut the afterbirth, cutting it at the nail until the moisture that is inside comes out. Then press on the woman's belly until the baby comes down. And if it does not come down, then give her an enema of fenugreek with oil of cumin; then have her drink a potion and sneeze several times, holding her mouth and nose for an hour: the baby will now come out. And if both hands come out first, then gently press on them one after the other. And if they cannot be pressed in, then have the woman sit on a stool and lift her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground and cover her, making sure she does not fall when standing up. And if the hands still cannot be inserted, and the baby is dead, then cut off its hands with the knife that is shown below and extract the baby, pressing equally.

The ruptures of the stomach are big, medium, and small;
Sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude from a large wound, causing intromission (insertion) of them.
And suturing is more difficult, and sometimes a small wound is worse than a large one,
because the intestines are put back in place with greater difficulty, unless they are replaced piece by piece while still hot;[8](https://fr.wiktionary.org/wiki/chaut#Ancien_fran%C3%A7ais) Because the intestines swell immediately when they feel the cold, making it more difficult to put them back in place.
And so it is better for the surgeon to twist [his hand] when making an incision, so that he can better set the intestines in their place, than for them to lie among the other [organs].

Of arrows
Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and the parts of the body where they land.
The diversity of arrows is such that there are some which have large points, and small ones, feathered and unfeathered. and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments; and that which falls in a member does so in two ways: either in the principal part,
such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestines, bladder, and similar members.[ When it falls in any part of these members, and the signs of death that I will tell you appear:[ then you must be careful about extracting this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions;[ and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
And the signs of the brain when the arrow falls and pierces the bone, and the dura mater that is above the brain, is when there is scotoma (partial vision loss) and stiffness and dizziness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of bile. And perhaps there is loss of strength in the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses speech and voice. and when there is an exit wound with whitish moisture resembling pus, and it oozes out like bruised flesh.[References:](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moyen_%C3%A2ge)
And if these signs appear to you, then refrain from treating [the wound], and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
The signs of the arrow when it falls or sticks are that it is close to the left breast, and it feels as if it is stuck in a hard thing, not hollow. And perhaps the arrow moves like the pulse, and black blood comes out, and cold sweats and cold shivering follow, along with fainting. Then know for certain that death is at hand.

of the shoulder fracture
It rarely happens that the shoulder breaks in such a way that it is not noticeable except by touch; one must prepare for the fracture according to its shape and relocate it according to its natural form, in all ways possible; then place on top of it powdered flour with plenty of egg whites, and light bandages, and put a double cloth over it; then put on a wide and thin plate, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate at any part of the shoulder, stuff those hairs with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then bind it tightly with a large bandage, making sure the plate does not move from its place, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and ensure the plate is in its correct position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. of the break in the neck.
Sometimes there occurs a break in the bones of the neck, and rarely does it bend; and also at the spine in the back. And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will recover or not, look and see if their hands are softened, swollen, and numb, and if they cannot move or extend them, and if you poke them with a needle, and they do not feel it. Know that they are in a critical condition in many ways, and if they can move them and feel when they are pinched and poked, know that the joints of the bone are safe, and that the patient will recover if treated.
And if such a thing happens to the spine of the back, and you want to know if it will heal or not, see if the feet are weak, and if there are symptoms present that are in the hands, and on the back there is a windiness and involuntary evacuation; and when it has been laid on its stomach, there is still involuntary evacuation. And when it is turned over on its back and it wants to move, it cannot. Know that it is fatal: do not labor in its care.
And if these symptoms do not occur, then the matter is easier.
And the treatment is as follows: if there is a hot abscess on the spine, place roses oil or egg yolk oil on it until it calms down; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and let them not sleep on the side where they feel pain, until it is healed. The breaking of the arm.
The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one of which is small and it is the one that follows the wrist; and the other is large and it is the one that is below, towards the little finger; perhaps the large foscile breaks alone, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
When the small ribs are broken, the restoration and healing is easy; and when the large ones are broken, the healing is difficult and more severe than when both are broken together. If it is only the small rib that is broken, then it should be lightly stretched and aligned.
And if it is the large rib, then it must be pulled more forcefully; and it should be stretched out on a cushion, and the pouchet of the hand held higher than the others, and the little fingers lower than the other fingers, and have the patient cross their arms over themselves with one cushion before them that is higher than what the patient can bear. Then, have the assistants extend the patient's arms on either side, either under their hand or with a bandage, and another assistant above. And then the physician should align it properly, according to its best form.
And if the break has pieces, then put each one in its place, and if there is any piece that pricks the heart and cannot be restored to its place, then saw through it and remove it as we have said before.
And if there is a wound with the break, I have spoken about this in a separate chapter; then take care of it (attend to it).
And if in the beginning of the setting, boils occur, then place a piece of linen cloth dipped in a mixture of rose oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and gently place a cloth over it, until the boils have subsided. Then remove the adhesive, and apply the plaster made from the powder of the mill with plenty of egg, then place the stylets, and let the stylet of the breakage be stronger and slightly larger than the others; and know that it should have six stylets or branches in several dispositions: either the breaker is in one of the bones, or in two; and bind more above the breakage than any other part, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are above the breakage be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the thread from which it is bound be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said. And wrap the member and the binding after several days. And if any misfortune befalls the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is necessary to rinse the member with warm water until the itching has subsided; and let the member not rest tightly. And then resume binding, and if the binding is weakened and the bones have separated, and similar things, then address it.
And if you notice that the circulation does not come to the member because it is too tight, then you should soften it slightly and leave it like that for several days, until the circulation returns, and then bind it.[1]
And if none of the things we have mentioned happen to the patient, then do not unbind them for twenty days or more. Instead, during this time, they should keep their hands on their neck with equal collars and be careful of movement and agitation, and sleep on their backs. And know that this breakage is healed in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps even in twenty days, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.

of bruises that appear on the suture

When the fracture of the bone is healed, but the limb remains weak and fragile afterward, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly and not properly; another reason is that there were too many bandages, preventing blood flow to the member; or due to excessive swelling; or from too much movement at the wrong time; or because the body has little blood, making it weak.
And the treatment is that you should feed the patient and make the body supple so that blood multiplies within it; and administer baths, and bring joy and pleasure to them; then apply poultices on the limb, such that the poultice draws a lot of blood to it, and often irrigate the area with warm water, until circulation returns to the member; and the member regains its natural appearance.
the crooked limb after being healed
When the member is crooked after being healed, and the bone is visibly broken, and the shape of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function; do not believe those who say that the limb should be broken again, as many foolish surgeons have done in our land; this practice is to be condemned, causing great harm, and possibly even death; however, if there are knots and tension, then they should be irrigated with warm water or softening herbs like those from the plant viscum album, including roots and melilotus; and make a softening plaster such as a well-made diachylon, take vinca leaves, infuse it in goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster with that; or use figs and pork lard, grind them up with cow dung, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
And sometimes, the knot (nodation) is removed by continuously and lengthily rubbing with hands wet (moistenous). And let the affected limb be moved/exercised every hour.
And if the twisted parts (tortuositez) are swollen and hardened, like stone, and it is necessary to remove it with iron, then one must cut it down to the bone using a sharp, light incision; and place cotton and bandages during treatment.
Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation is caused by the displacement of a joint from its place, which prevents movement and results in deformity of the limb, causing the patient great pain and injury.[STH: Added missing word "caused" for better readability.]
When a dislocation occurs, it must be corrected immediately.
For if one delays, the place will swell, and perhaps it cannot be reset; therefore, it is not at all appropriate to move it when it is swollen: often it brings forth spasms and other pains.
Nevertheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then leave them until the abscess has subsided; then apply hot water and oil to the limb, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into place.
And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from head to foot.
of the jaw[ fem. noun, plural form: mandibules ]
It rarely happens that the jaw becomes dislocated on both sides, and there are two ways in which this dislocation can occur: either they are slightly pulled out of place and become somewhat loose; or they become completely dislocated and hang towards the chin, causing saliva to flow from the mouth that the person cannot hold back, and they cannot close their mouth or enunciate clearly, as their tongue is trapped.  [Note: I made an educated guess for the word "envoloupe" which can mean either "wrapped" or "involved". Given the context, I chose "trapped"]
When a dislocation is small, it can return to its place through several positions.
And if it is complete, you should quickly reset it and not delay.
And in such a way that the attendant holds the head of the patient, and places the tip of one of his hands into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is two-sided; and the other hand should be free to adjust and make it even. Command the patient to relax and move their jaws in all directions.
And the physician should make it even, until it returns to its place.
And if the returning is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, soak them with hot water and oil, until you easily reset it; do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
And when they are evenly reset, and the patient's mouth closes well without difficulty, place dampened bandages on it, made of a mixture of rose oil and wax, then lightly bind it with soft ligaments;
and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head resting between two cushions, so that it is not moved to the right or left, nor should they try to forcefully chew, but eat light food until the pains are gone, and the jaw joints are healed;
and then eat what they want lightly, and do not strain to open their mouth while eating or drinking, until the jaw joint is fully healed and healthy.[stop request] Sure! And if the two jawbones cannot be properly reset in an hour and are not returned to their proper position, then fever and swelling may result, and possibly stomach inflammation, and perhaps vomiting of bile.
And when you see this, then know that it is a lost cause; and many times those to whom it happens die within 9 days.
of the fork (or pincher)
The "fork" cannot be dislodged from the side next to the ribs and the bladder, and it is sometimes dislodged out of place, which can be felt.
And the treatment is as follows: have the patient lie down with their back flat on the ground, extend their arms, and then firmly press on the area with your palm, and it will return to its proper position. Then apply a poultice and bandage and bind it.
And the head of the shoulder that is dislocated towards the back cannot be moved. If it can, and if it becomes dislodged at any time, then reset it in its proper place as we have said. Then apply a poultice and bandage and bind it, and tell the patient to rest until they are healed.
And similarly, bring back the shoulder blade when it is dislocated from its place.
of the dislocation of the shoulder
Know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways only: of which one is when it dislocates at the side of the scapula below; and the second is at the part of the armpit; and sometimes it dislocates above, but this happens rarely.
And it should not dislocate backwards by the shoulder, nor should it dislocate inside because of nerves; and more often than not, it dislocates downward towards the scapula, especially for those who have little flesh, as it slips out quickly; but for those who have enough flesh, it does not slip out easily, and it goes back in place with difficulty.
And sometimes it happens to some men that they receive a shock or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.[Please note that "desaluee" in the provided text is not grammatically correct. It should be "desaloiée", which means "dislocated". I will use the correct form in my translation below.]
Then you should try it, until you are certain; and only then should you begin the cure.
And a dislocation is recognized when it is lowered towards the shoulder blade, and there is a noticeable difference between the healthy and sickened shoulder, and you will find clear differences between them. and you will find at the top of the shoulder a pit (or depression), and under the shoulder blade when touching the top of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor make any movements.
And also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it clearly when touching.[STH1]: The abbreviation "STH1" was not used in the provided text. If this is a continuation of a previous prompt, please provide the full context. If this is a new prompt, please clarify the meaning of "STH1".
And this type of dislocation is not difficult to correct when it is new, or in the case of infants being sick.
And the manner is that the servant raises the patient's hand up high, then puts your feet under the pelvis, and pulls the joint with force up to the place; and the servant lifts the hand, and stretches it up, then puts it down; it will come quickly.
And if it does not come as we have said many days after, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and give them soothing and relaxing remedies, such as a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in water, and let them take it.
Then lay the patient down on their back, and place a soft woolen cushion under the pelvis, not too hard or too soft, then put the patient's heel on the cushion and lift the shoulder with strength, and pull the hand of the afflicted person;
and have another servant hold the head of the patient, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder will come back into place immediately, and if you see that it is dislocated, reset it in this manner:
and make sure there is a person present who is bigger than the patient; and let them stand to the patient's side, and push their shoulder under the patient's armpit, and lift the armpit up high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and let another assistant pull the patient's hand down towards their belly. And if the patient is too lightweight, have them hold onto something heavy, and with this, the dislocation should return to its proper position now.
And another way to reset it is as follows: take a long stake and drive it into the ground, so that the head of the stake is about the same size as a fist, and neither too thick nor too thin; then place it underneath the patient, but make sure they have soft blankets or cloths beneath them, and let the patient be lying lengthwise along the stake. Then stretch out their hand on the other side, and the joint will quickly return to its proper position.
And if it does not want to return due to all the things we have mentioned, perform this cure: take a splinter of 2 arms length and 4 fingers width, which has a pointed end to enter deep underneath the dislocation, in this manner:
then place a soft cloth over the wood so that the wood does not injure the patient, then place it under the dislocation of the patient; and stretch the arm out along the length of the wood, and tie the shoulder to the wood, and the arm at the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on a step of a ladder wide enough, and let the hand hang down, and leave the body hanging from the other side; the joint will return in this way.
And when it is back in place, no matter how, you should then place underneath the dislocation a sphere of wool equal [in size], then apply ointment made with powder from the mill, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then bind it under the dislocation appropriately, and turn the binding over the ointment, and bring the hand to touch the neck, and let the hand remain in this way.
And it is necessary that he eats only liquids until the limb feels better, as it will heal faster; and then eat solid food after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is firm and not softened, then it has healed.
And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, then you should apply cauteries at three openings, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries.
And if you do all of this, and it becomes dislocated again after seven days, and the joint cannot hold and the arm cannot be raised, then you should know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder have been cut or stretched or weakened; and you should know that the joint will never return to its place.
A dislocation that is to the side of the hip, or the breasts, or the back, is caused by impact and extension of the hands, and another joint is used as a replacement; and it should be treated until it has healed.[ original text was "i aministre on autre lieure" which I translated as "and another joint is used as a replacement". Other possible translation for this phrase could be "and an alternative method is applied"]
And if after the healing there comes cracking in the limb and difficulty moving, then the patient should take many baths until the cracking has subsided and the limb returns to its normal state.
of the dislocation of the rib(s)
Know that the joint of the rib is dislocated at points, and returns to those points; it is dislocated all around, both in front and back, and the dislocation has not been corrected, for it is clearly visible and can be felt; and it is dislocated according to each shape. And when you align the affected rib with the healthy one, it can be clearly seen. For the joint is misaligned and the patient cannot bend their arm or touch their shoulder at all.
And it must be set in such a way that abscesses do not develop there, for if abscesses were to form there, setting it would be difficult and perhaps impossible to fully reset, especially when it is dislocated in the back; this type of dislocation is worse than others, and more painful, and may even lead to death.
And the restoration, when it is of such a nature that it can be reset, is as follows: you stretch out your two hands and hold his arms spread wide, with the doctor's hands placed around the rib both above and below, pressing the joint back into place at its roots or the base of the palm until it returns to its original position.
And if the dislocation is in front, it comes back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the displaced joint.
And if it does not want to return to its place, administer strong extension; and this is done by two people extending the arm, and holding it with two people, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side after you have wrapped a long and wide cloth around it.
And when the surgeon has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then strongly pushes the joint until it comes back.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
And when it is in its place, apply dry emplaster with egg white, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for several days, then loosen it.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
And if the joint is firm in its place, loosen the binding and let it be; but if you see that the joint is not tightly bound, reapply the dressing and binding, and leave it for several days until it is firmly set; then loosen it.[^1](#footnote_inline_1_0)
And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until he is eased; or put sheep fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath; And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then replace the fat, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung warmed with butter, and bind it on. Thus will it return to its proper position.
the dislocation of the hand
The joint of the hand has become dislocated, and the recovery is quicker than for other joints. Nevertheless, it should be returned to its place quickly, in the same hour that it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen, or there comes a hot abscess.
And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and position the patient's palm so that it is aligned with the appearance of the joint, then apply pressure until it aligns.
Nevertheless, you must ensure that it is in the correct position; then have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and realignment. And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, then have the patient place the back of their hand on the table and the assistant place their hand over the appearance of the joint. If it aligns now, that's good.[
If not, bind it with soothing plasters for abscesses and leave it like that without further movement.
And if he cannot endure it, and you cannot set it in place after several days, then the joint remains dislocated.
And it does not harm the patient as long as his hand remains moist and cannot grasp anything. Then know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other means except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps it will be of no use.
And when the hand is in place, put on the emplaster that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.[Reader's note: The author is discussing the treatment of a dislocated finger or toe, suggesting to use an emplaster and then bind it in place for 5 days before removing the bandage. This is an example of medieval medical practices, where treatments were often based on observation and experience rather than scientific evidence.]
And if he cannot move it well and there is any cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and massage it until it heals.[Reader's note: The author is still discussing the treatment of a dislocated finger or toe. They suggest using warm water to help reduce stiffness and promote healing in case of any cracks or injuries.]
of the dislocation of the fingers.
Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the stomach;
Then stretch the finger and push the dislocation back into its socket until it pops back in, then hold the base of the finger and bend it towards the direction where it is disjointed.
And leave it for two days, then straighten it on that day, and wrap it with a bandage as we have said, and unwrap it during the day, and make it move, and re-bandage it at night; and do this frequently until it becomes firm.
And do the same if it is dislocated at the stomach of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it heals; and do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
The dislocation of the spine of the back.
When the swelling of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death quickly approaches the patient.
And the sign is that stools leave suddenly without willingness, and cannot be held back, and often some members become weak, or both thighs or both arms or one.
And often the swelling moves in four parts; the one that moves to the back is called "gilbositez".
The treatment is to determine if "gilbositez" has come from childhood, in which case there is no cure or complete healing.
And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients said there were great cures for it in grand words, but there is not always great benefit in all of them.[IST] mes je vos di et confesse que la bone maniere de cure est par le moyen de l’incision, car elle delivre et eschappe toute la region du ventre, et les autres membres qui sont entour.
but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in diverse ways. \\"
I say that in the swelling (gill-boils) that comes to the breast, there is no remedy or cure.
and also that which comes directly in two ribs, and cannot be cured unless it is the one that comes to the back, as I say.[Translate the following text:] Certes, je l’ai veu estre et le tens que je ai este en service de mon seignor, si come il me souvient, et quant j’estois a Constantinople, et fu es anz de grant faim.
And it is that the patient should be stretched out on their back evenly and have something to support them underneath so as not to injure themselves;[Translate the following text:] Et se la char engroissie et li malaides ne peut tolerer ke li ventres soit aplaniez, si fet il couper la chair ou il est engrossie.
Then insert a stake into the ground near the head and another by the feet, and tie a rope under the soles of the patient's feet, and another around their haunches, and knees, and ankles;[Translate the following text:] Et quant la char est coupee et la plaie nettié et li sains espanduz dedenz, si fet il crever le pis de l’autre part.
and two assistants shall know the ties, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two fire-sticks;
and let them be tightly bound, the fire-sticks as we have said, and let the surgeon place his palms firmly on the spine until it recovers.
And if it does not recover by this treatment, take a board of three arms length, and have it hollowed out underneath, and let the patient be on his side, and place the head of the board beneath the opening, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the surgeon put his feet on the other end of the board and press firmly until it returns to its place; and if necessary, use a device that turns by hand.
And you shall place two fire-sticks at the head of the patient, one arm's length long, and two others towards the feet, and between each stick there should be a handspan of space.
and have in each stake a hole, where the tourniquet runs, and have the stakes firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between every two stakes have one turning stake, on which the ties turn, and have in the two turnings two small stakes of a palm's length, to turn the turning stake;
and then tie the tie that is between the saddle to the turning stake towards the head, and the other tie towards the feet at the other turning stake, and each of the assistants turns his turning stake to the full length of the tie, and the master places the needle evenly as we have said.
And when it is even, put on a desiccative plaster with an abundance of egg, and then the wicks, and then the style of a tablet of 3 fingers long, which reaches the area of gout and the healthy part of the shoulder blade, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and treat the patient with subtle care until it is healed.
and if something arises at the end of the healing, then it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines, with the style that we have mentioned before; and sometimes a piece of wood is administered.
and sometimes there appears in the lower spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that shows, due to which one should not assume: perhaps it would bring about death.
of hip dislocations
Know that the hip joints and shoulder joints do not come out of place except for dislocations, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint can become dislocated in four ways: inwardly, outwardly, forward, and backward; and more so inwardly than otherwise, and slightly out of place in front and back.
And the recognition of an inward dislocation is that when the affected leg is joined with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the affected knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the affected patient cannot bend their knee over the fire.[translator's note: it is mentioned that the patient is unable to bend their knee while sitting near a fire as a sign of an inward dislocation] and the area next to it is swollen due to abscess, because the head of the thigh bone moves there.[translator's note: The text suggests that the swelling occurs because the head of the femur (thigh bone) has moved towards the area due to dislocation.][IST] Et quant la jambe est desaloiee devant, li cuissiaus vient au leu ou l’os de la hanche reposa por coi il ne se puet muevre, et plus se montre cels que li sains;
And the sign of that which is about to happen to him, is that these symptoms are contrary to those before.
And the sign of that which is about to happen, is that he stretches his leg well according to its full length; nonetheless, he does not bend the knee without pain, and if one wants him to walk, he cannot advance, and he holds his urine, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he lifts himself up on his heel.
And the sign of that which has already happened, is that he cannot stretch or bend his knee, and one leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the femur is located below the ribcage.
The reduction of this type of dislocation is as follows: observe whether the dislocation is old and persists in its position, then there is no need for treatment and one should not be overconfident.
And in the case of a fresh dislocation, which can be of four types, one should act quickly to return the joint to its place and stretch it both inside and outside, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return to its place and there is no need for further treatment.
And if it does not come back in this way, you should prepare for one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with a strap tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand in such a way that they place their hands beneath the patient's armpits, then bind them with a gentle strap above the thigh; and another holds the head of the strap.
And they extend upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground in one motion, and remains hanging.[Additional context: This passage describes a procedure for reducing a dislocated shoulder, involving several assistants to hold the patient in place while resetting the joint.]
This method of extension is common in four cases, and if the dislocation has been reduced as we have said, that is good.
If not, you should attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the side, you should often turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the strap on the root of the thigh and the joint that is beneath the groin, and then pull the strap upwards toward the groin and toward the armpit;
then take another assistant and hold the patient's arms, hug the patient's hip girdle, and stretch it out very much: it will return to its place now; and this type of dislocation is easier than others.
And if you cannot hold it in place in this manner as we have said, then it is necessary to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong but soft ligament at the heels and knees, and keep the affected leg extended two fingers more than the other.
Then have them hang by the head from a beam and be two arms' length off the ground; then command one assistant to hug the head of the thigh and have another assistant hanging with the patient, who will strongly hug the thigh, for the joint will return quickly now.
And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down as we have said in the one with gout, and tie a ligament on the affected leg properly, and also on the foot.
then place two hot irons, one at the head and one at the feet, then insert one hot iron between the thighs of the patient in a horizontal manner; and have cloths soaked in water placed around [the patient], so as not to burn them, then each assistant should extend towards the patient, and the doctor should place his hand evenly on the dislocation.
If it [the dislocation] returns to its place, that is good. If not, place a board under it and press as we have said in the section on paralysis, and let the patient lie on their healthy side.[OT: It is unclear what "it" refers to in the first sentence (the dislocation or the limb). I assumed it was the dislocation. If it refers to the limb then the translation would be: "If it [the limb] returns to its place, that is good. If not..." ]
And when the dislocation is in front [of the body], one must quickly stretch out the affected leg as I have said; and the doctor should take care to be over the bad groin, then press with his other hand and pull downwards towards the knee.
And if the dislocation is on the side, one must not stretch out the patient downwards nor lift them up from the ground, instead they should be in the same position as if their haunch was dislocated to the side, just as we have said about lying on both haunches. And let it be above its position, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table;
It will be done when the patient stretches out their legs and they are even; then adjust the thighs, and apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the swelling does not move;
And let him rest for three or four days, then loosen it and apply the poultice again; and if you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three more days; then loosen it and make him walk gently until the limb is strengthened.
of the dislocation of the knee.
The knee becomes dislocated in three ways: namely, inside and outside, and backward; but never in front.[Note: Dislocation of the knee in the front is anatomically impossible]
And the signs are that you tell the patient to bend his leg at his hip, and if it does not bend at his hip, know that it is dislocated.
And the restoration of all [dislocations] is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back against his face, and place his foot on top of your feet.
Then take his knee with your palms, and pull it towards you between your arms, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and have another assistant stretch out his foot until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he can easily bend his leg at his hip.
And apply the poultice and heat the leg against the hip, and bind the limbs together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient must not move or walk until the limb is healed.
And if the limb is not healing, apply strong extension as we have said in the treatment of inflammation, until it is healed.
of the dislocation of the heel.
The heel is sometimes dislocated and sometimes completely misaligned, both inside and outside.
And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen and tends to bulge towards the side where it is dislocated.
The reduction (of the dislocation) is easy and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9duction\_orthop%C3%A9dique](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/R%C3%A9duction_orthop%C3%A9dique)
And when it is dislocated completely, you should make the patient sit upright and have one assistant hold them by the leg, above the ankle.
then pull the foot toward you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards, and properly push the foot upward;
and do this two times, as we have said, by pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns to its place, that is good; if not, then begin the task again, for it will return.
and if it cannot return to its place in this way, then have the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and firmly plant a stake in the ground between their thighs, and tie cloth around it so that it does not injure the patient;
then one minister should hold the thigh, and another minister should extend the foot with their hands or using a strap, tying it to the neck of the foot;[ST1] Then one minister should grasp the thigh, and another minister should stretch out the leg with his hands or with a band, which he should tie around the neck of the foot. then have each minister stretch out evenly, and the stake should still be between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when being stretched.
then place the doctor evenly the dislocation in his hands, and another minister holds the healthy leg below, and the dislocation will come back quickly.
And when it is ready, apply the poultice and bandages firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and watch the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the binding is not too tight.
then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, tighten them; then undo the binding on the third or fourth day, and forbid the patient to walk for four days; and if he goes before this time limit, it is not safe that it will not dislocate again.
And if abscesses come, you must calm them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
of the shoulders
When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
And if the dislocation is in any part of the back or leg, you should make the patient sit on a flat bed or on a table, straight up, and place your foot on the visible joints. Then press firmly with your foot until it returns to its proper position.[STT\_1]
And when it is aligned and there's nothing visible, place a two-legged table under the sole of your foot, then apply strong pressure and leave it for three days before loosening it. Allow the patient to rest until they are healed.[STT\_1]
regarding wound and dislocation together
When a wound comes with a dislocation, and one wants to reset it, it often happens that the patient dies.
And do not be overconfident in treating it if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful, and slow, not quick.
And at the beginning, use soothing treatments for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery. And when you see hope, then reset the limb in its place now, so that the hot abscess comes there.
And when the limb is in place, then administer soothing treatments for the hot abscess and treat the wound as it should be, with drying ointments.[STHAP: I translated "d'oignemens desiccatis" as "with drying ointments", because "desiccatis" comes from the Latin verb "desiccare" which means to dry out. ]
and if with the dislocation there is a break and small bones disjoined, set the bones, and do what we have said in simple illnesses;
and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it will be harmful to you according to your Creator, and for the safety of your weapons and body. Amen.
